###begin article-title 0
###xml 72 91 72 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 72 91 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
The Complete Genome Sequence and Analysis of the Epsilonproteobacterium Arcobacter butzleri
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 453 461 453 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g001">Figure 1</xref>
Conceived and designed the experiments: WM CP. Performed the experiments: WM CP MR GW JM AR. Analyzed the data: WM CP DU PH JS MR GM MW TB JM AR. Contributed reagents/materials/analysis tools: WM CP MR JM AR. Wrote the paper: WM CP JS GM MW. Other: Initiated the project, Final assembly and annotation, Comparative genomic analyses: WM. Construction of DNA microarray and DNA microarray analysis: CP. Shotgun sequencing and assembly: MR JM AR. Designed Figure 1 for the manuscript: DU TB PH. Gap closure sequencing: GW. Secured funds to support the study: LS RM.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
Background
###end title 2
###begin p 3
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 146 166 146 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter jejuni</italic>
###xml 171 190 171 190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter pylori</italic>
###xml 268 279 268 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 0 19 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
###xml 146 166 <span type="species:ncbi:197">Campylobacter jejuni</span>
###xml 171 190 <span type="species:ncbi:210">Helicobacter pylori</span>
###xml 244 249 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 268 279 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Arcobacter butzleri is a member of the epsilon subdivision of the Proteobacteria and a close taxonomic relative of established pathogens, such as Campylobacter jejuni and Helicobacter pylori. Here we present the complete genome sequence of the human clinical isolate, A. butzleri strain RM4018.
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Methodology/Principal Findings
###end title 4
###begin p 5
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 39 57 39 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 120 146 120 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfuromonas denitrificans</italic>
###xml 151 173 151 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wolinella succinogenes</italic>
###xml 195 212 195 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 267 277 267 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurovum</italic>
###xml 282 295 282 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>
###xml 494 510 494 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. denitrificans</italic>
###xml 512 527 512 527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 529 539 529 539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurovum</italic>
###xml 548 561 548 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>
###xml 675 686 675 686 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 960 971 960 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 999 1010 999 1010 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1123 1134 1123 1134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1177 1188 1177 1188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 0 19 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
###xml 151 173 <span type="species:ncbi:844">Wolinella succinogenes</span>
###xml 494 510 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">S. denitrificans</span>
###xml 512 527 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 675 686 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 960 971 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 999 1010 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1123 1134 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1177 1188 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Arcobacter butzleri is a member of the Campylobacteraceae, but the majority of its proteome is most similar to those of Sulfuromonas denitrificans and Wolinella succinogenes, both members of the Helicobacteraceae, and those of the deep-sea vent Epsilonproteobacteria Sulfurovum and Nitratiruptor. In addition, many of the genes and pathways described here, e.g. those involved in signal transduction and sulfur metabolism, have been identified previously within the epsilon subdivision only in S. denitrificans, W. succinogenes, Sulfurovum, and/or Nitratiruptor, or are unique to the subdivision. In addition, the analyses indicated also that a substantial proportion of the A. butzleri genome is devoted to growth and survival under diverse environmental conditions, with a large number of respiration-associated proteins, signal transduction and chemotaxis proteins and proteins involved in DNA repair and adaptation. To investigate the genomic diversity of A. butzleri strains, we constructed an A. butzleri DNA microarray comprising 2238 genes from strain RM4018. Comparative genomic indexing analysis of 12 additional A. butzleri strains identified both the core genes of A. butzleri and intraspecies hypervariable regions, where <70% of the genes were present in at least two strains.
###end p 5
###begin title 6
Conclusion/Significance
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 145 156 145 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 145 156 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
The presence of pathways and loci associated often with non-host-associated organisms, as well as genes associated with virulence, suggests that A. butzleri is a free-living, water-borne organism that might be classified rightfully as an emerging pathogen. The genome sequence and analyses presented in this study are an important first step in understanding the physiology and genetics of this organism, which constitutes a bridge between the environment and mammalian hosts.
###end p 7
###begin title 8
Introduction
###end title 8
###begin p 9
###xml 125 143 125 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 145 162 145 162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 167 179 167 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nautiliaceae</italic>
###xml 307 320 307 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 322 332 322 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 337 353 337 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurospirillum</italic>
###xml 361 379 361 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 385 397 385 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 402 411 402 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wolinella</italic>
###xml 419 436 419 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 481 501 481 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter jejuni</italic>
###xml 501 504 501 504 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Skirrow1">[1]</xref>
###xml 509 528 509 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter pylori</italic>
###xml 528 531 528 531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Marshall1">[2]</xref>
###xml 593 618 593 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter upsaliensis</italic>
###xml 618 621 618 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Sandstedt1">[3]</xref>
###xml 626 647 626 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter mustelae</italic>
###xml 647 650 647 650 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Fox1">[4]</xref>
###xml 699 715 699 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurospirillum</italic>
###xml 721 724 721 724 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Vandamme1">[5]</xref>
###xml 481 501 <span type="species:ncbi:197">Campylobacter jejuni</span>
###xml 509 528 <span type="species:ncbi:210">Helicobacter pylori</span>
###xml 593 618 <span type="species:ncbi:28080">Campylobacter upsaliensis</span>
###xml 626 647 <span type="species:ncbi:217">Helicobacter mustelae</span>
The epsilon subdivision of the Gram-negative Proteobacteria comprises multiple genera contained within three major families: Campylobacteraceae, Helicobacteraceae and Nautiliaceae. The majority of well-characterized species in this subdivision are members of genera within the first two families, including Campylobacter, Arcobacter and Sulfurospirillum in the Campylobacteraceae, and Helicobacter and Wolinella in the Helicobacteraceae. Many of these species are pathogenic, e.g. Campylobacter jejuni[1] and Helicobacter pylori[2], and/or are associated with a particular host or hosts, e.g. Campylobacter upsaliensis[3] and Helicobacter mustelae[4]; however, several species are free-living, e.g. Sulfurospirillum spp. [5], and they are not considered to be pathogenic.
###end p 9

###xml 284 299 284 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. nitrofigilis</italic>
###xml 299 302 299 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-McClung1">[9]</xref>
###xml 304 315 304 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 317 333 317 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. cryaerophilus</italic>
###xml 338 350 338 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. skirrowii</italic>
###xml 394 398 394 398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 406 421 406 421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. nitrofigilis</italic>
###xml 478 498 478 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Spartina aterniflora</italic>
###xml 527 530 527 530 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-McClung1">[9]</xref>

###xml 727 731 727 731 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Donachie1">[11]</xref>

###xml 802 826 802 826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Candidatus A. sulfidicus</italic>

###xml 1112 1116 1112 1116 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Prabagaran1">[15]</xref>
###xml 1153 1157 1153 1157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Grabowski1">[16]</xref>
###xml 1191 1195 1191 1195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-FriasLopez1">[17]</xref>
###xml 1216 1220 1216 1220 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Thamdrup1">[18]</xref>
###xml 1233 1237 1233 1237 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Naganuma1">[19]</xref>
###xml 1256 1260 1256 1260 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Snaidr1">[20]</xref>
###xml 1303 1307 1303 1307 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-McGarvey1">[21]</xref>
###xml 1441 1452 1441 1452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1454 1470 1454 1470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. cryaerophilus</italic>
###xml 1475 1487 1475 1487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. skirrowii</italic>
###xml 1611 1615 1611 1615 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Assanta1">[22]</xref>
###xml 1616 1620 1616 1620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Stampi1">[30]</xref>
###xml 227 238 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 243 259 <span type="species:ncbi:28198">A. cryaerophilus</span>
###xml 264 276 <span type="species:ncbi:28200">A. skirrowii</span>
###xml 284 299 <span type="species:ncbi:28199">A. nitrofigilis</span>
###xml 304 315 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 317 333 <span type="species:ncbi:28198">A. cryaerophilus</span>
###xml 338 350 <span type="species:ncbi:28200">A. skirrowii</span>
###xml 387 393 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 406 421 <span type="species:ncbi:28199">A. nitrofigilis</span>
###xml 659 672 <span type="species:ncbi:197482">A. halophilus</span>
###xml 736 747 <span type="species:ncbi:255507">A. cibarius</span>
###xml 813 826 <span type="species:ncbi:162154">A. sulfidicus</span>
###xml 1222 1232 <span type="species:ncbi:6426">tube worms</span>
###xml 1441 1452 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1454 1470 <span type="species:ncbi:28198">A. cryaerophilus</span>
###xml 1475 1487 <span type="species:ncbi:28200">A. skirrowii</span>
The genus Arcobacter is an unusual taxon within the epsilon subdivision in that it contains both pathogenic and free-living species found in a wide range of environments. Currently, Arcobacter contains four recognized species: A. butzleri[6], A. cryaerophilus[7], A. skirrowii[8] and A. nitrofigilis[9]. A. butzleri, A. cryaerophilus and A. skirrowii have been isolated from animals and humans [10], while A. nitrofigilis is a nitrogen-fixing bacterium isolated originally from Spartina aterniflora roots in an estuarine marsh [9]. In addition to these established Arcobacter species, three new species have been described recently: 1) the obligate halophile A. halophilus sp. nov., isolated from a Hawaiian hypersaline lagoon [11], 2) A. cibarius sp. nov., isolated from broiler carcasses [12] and 3) Candidatus A. sulfidicus, a sulfide-oxidizing marine organism that produces filamentous sulfur [13]. In addition, several potential, novel Arcobacter species, based so far on only 16S rDNA sequence data, have been identified in: the flora of deep-sea hydrothermal vents [14], hydrocarbon-contaminated seawater [15], a low-salinity petroleum reservoir [16], infected or dead coral surfaces [17], deep-sea sediments [18], tube worms [19], anaerobic sludge [20], and a circulated dairy wastewater lagoon [21]. These studies demonstrate clearly that the genus is associated strongly with fresh-water and marine environments. In fact, although A. butzleri, A. cryaerophilus and A. skirrowii have been isolated often from animals or food sources, they have been isolated frequently also from water or water systems [22]-[30].
###end p 10

###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 66 77 66 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 113 117 113 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 172 185 172 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 234 245 234 245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 250 263 250 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 310 323 310 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 337 353 337 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. cryaerophilus</italic>
###xml 353 357 353 357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 359 370 359 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 473 484 473 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 540 544 540 544 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 620 633 620 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 688 692 676 680 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Mandrell1">[31]</xref>
###xml 702 713 690 701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 841 845 811 815 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 860 871 830 841 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 903 916 873 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 967 971 937 941 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 0 19 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
###xml 66 77 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 234 245 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 337 353 <span type="species:ncbi:28198">A. cryaerophilus</span>
###xml 359 370 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 473 484 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 702 713 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 860 871 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Arcobacter butzleri is the best characterized of all Arcobacters. A. butzleri cells are small, spiral and motile [10], similar morphologically to the taxonomically-related Campylobacter. Nonetheless, notable differences exist between A. butzleri and Campylobacter spp. Classified initially as an "aerotolerant Campylobacter", along with A. cryaerophilus[10], A. butzleri is able to grow aerobically, at variance with most Campylobacters which are microaerophilic. However, A. butzleri grows also under microaerobic and anaerobic conditions [10]; thus, this bacterium can grow at all oxygen concentrations. Additionally, Campylobacter spp. grow generally between 37degreesC and 42degreesC [31], whereas A. butzleri is more psychrophilic with a temperature range between 15degreesC and 37degreesC, although some strains can grow at 42degreesC [10]. Furthermore, A. butzleri is more halotolerant than most Campylobacter spp., with some strains able to grow at 3.5% NaCl [10].
###end p 11

###xml 6 17 6 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>

###xml 176 180 176 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Rivas1">[34]</xref>
###xml 200 204 200 204 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Atabay1">[35]</xref>
###xml 206 210 206 210 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Houf2">[36]</xref>
###xml 229 233 229 233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Manke1">[37]</xref>
###xml 254 258 254 258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Golla1">[38]</xref>
###xml 260 264 260 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Wesley1">[39]</xref>
###xml 271 275 271 275 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Rivas1">[34]</xref>
###xml 307 311 307 311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-vanDriessche1">[40]</xref>
###xml 313 324 313 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Engberg1">[41]</xref>
###xml 401 405 401 405 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Vandenberg1">[47]</xref>
###xml 449 460 449 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 520 524 520 524 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 535 546 535 546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 589 593 589 593 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Lau1">[48]</xref>
###xml 595 599 595 599 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Yan1">[49]</xref>
###xml 624 628 624 628 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-ProuzetMauleon1">[46]</xref>
###xml 734 738 734 738 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Vandenberg1">[47]</xref>
###xml 1145 1149 1145 1149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Houf3">[50]</xref>
###xml 1193 1209 1193 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. cryaerophilus</italic>
###xml 1211 1222 1211 1222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1270 1274 1270 1274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Vandenberg1">[47]</xref>
###xml 1294 1305 1294 1305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1426 1437 1426 1437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1619 1630 1619 1630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1655 1659 1655 1659 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 1689 1698 1689 1698 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 1916 1920 1916 1920 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-ProuzetMauleon1">[46]</xref>
###xml 6 17 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 144 148 <span type="species:ncbi:9823">pigs</span>
###xml 182 189 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">chicken</span>
###xml 313 324 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 366 371 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 449 460 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 535 546 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 672 677 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 975 983 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
###xml 1125 1130 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1193 1209 <span type="species:ncbi:28198">A. cryaerophilus</span>
###xml 1211 1222 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1294 1305 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1426 1437 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1558 1563 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1619 1630 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1689 1698 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 1806 1811 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
While A. butzleri is isolated often from aqueous environments, it is isolated also from multiple animals and food sources. It has been found in pigs [32] and ground pork [33], [34], chicken carcasses [35], [36] and other poultry [37], as well as in beef [38], [39], lamb [34] and the feces of other animals [40]. A. butzleri has also been isolated increasingly from human diarrheal stool samples [41]-[47]. The clinical symptomatology described for A. butzleri typically includes diarrhea and recurrent abdominal cramps [10], although A. butzleri-related bacteremia has also been reported [48], [49]. Prouzet-Mauleon et al. [46] reported an isolation frequency of 1% from human clinical stool samples. Additionally, Vandenberg et al. [47] reported an isolation frequency of 3.5% from diarrheic stool samples. Although co-infection with other enteric pathogens was reported by Prouzet-Mauleon and Vandenberg, in the majority of samples (14/15 clinical stool samples and 55/67 patients, respectively) no other enteric pathogen was detected. Houf et al. reported that Arcobacters were isolated from 1.4% (7/500) of asymptomatic human stool samples [50]. However, all seven isolates were typed as A. cryaerophilus; A. butzleri was not isolated. Similarly, Vandenberg et al. [47] reported also that A. butzleri was isolated more frequently from diarrheic stool samples than from non-diarrheic stool samples. Thus, the isolation of A. butzleri from diarrheic stool samples is likely to be relevant clinically and is probably not due to the organism being merely a human commensal. Therefore, these data suggest strongly that A. butzleri is an emerging pathogen [10], where transmission, as with C. jejuni, occurs probably through consumption of contaminated food or water. The low level of incidence reported in human clinical samples is most likely an underestimate, due to sub-optimal isolation and/or detection methods [46].
###end p 12

###xml 693 713 693 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter curvus</italic>

###xml 1068 1072 1068 1072 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Tomb1">[58]</xref>
###xml 1073 1077 1073 1077 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Oh1">[60]</xref>
###xml 1116 1140 1116 1140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter acinonychis</italic>
###xml 1155 1159 1155 1159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Eppinger1">[61]</xref>
###xml 1188 1201 1188 1201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>

###xml 1268 1272 1268 1272 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Nakagawa1">[62]</xref>
###xml 1345 1356 1345 1356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1471 1482 1471 1482 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1508 1526 1508 1526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 33 44 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 229 240 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 378 401 <span type="species:ncbi:32022">C. jejuni subsp. jejuni</span>
###xml 475 498 <span type="species:ncbi:32021">C. jejuni subsp. doylei</span>
###xml 527 559 <span type="species:ncbi:306254">Campylobacter coli strain RM2228</span>
###xml 561 593 <span type="species:ncbi:306263">Campylobacter lari strain RM2100</span>
###xml 598 612 <span type="species:ncbi:28080">C. upsaliensis</span>
###xml 633 678 <span type="species:ncbi:360106">Campylobacter fetus subsp. fetus strain 82-40</span>
###xml 693 727 <span type="species:ncbi:360105">Campylobacter curvus strain 525.92</span>
###xml 742 777 <span type="species:ncbi:360104">Campylobacter concisus strain 13826</span>
###xml 792 833 <span type="species:ncbi:360107">Campylobacter hominis strain ATCC BAA-381</span>
###xml 903 931 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">Thiomicrospira denitrificans</span>
###xml 948 986 <span type="species:ncbi:273121">Wolinella succinogenes strain DSM 1740</span>
###xml 993 1015 <span type="species:ncbi:32025">Helicobacter hepaticus</span>
###xml 1057 1066 <span type="species:ncbi:210">H. pylori</span>
###xml 1116 1154 <span type="species:ncbi:382638">Helicobacter acinonychis strain Sheeba</span>
###xml 1321 1326 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1345 1356 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1471 1482 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Relatively little is known about A. butzleri, compared to other members of the epsilon subdivision, but the wealth of genomic information from other epsilonproteobacterial taxa provides a solid foundation to compare and contrast A. butzleri to its taxonomic relatives. The genomes of multiple species of Epsilonproteobacteria have been sequenced; these include: four strains of C. jejuni subsp. jejuni ([51]-[54]: strains NCTC 11168, RM1221, 81-176 and 81116, respectively); C. jejuni subsp. doylei strain 269.97 (CP000768.1); Campylobacter coli strain RM2228, Campylobacter lari strain RM2100 and C. upsaliensis strain RM3195 [52]; Campylobacter fetus subsp. fetus strain 82-40 (CP000487.1); Campylobacter curvus strain 525.92 (CP000767.1); Campylobacter concisus strain 13826 (CP000792.1); Campylobacter hominis strain ATCC BAA-381 (CP000776.1); Sulfuromonas denitrificans strain ATCC 33889 (formerly Thiomicrospira denitrificans[55]: CP000153); Wolinella succinogenes strain DSM 1740 [56]; Helicobacter hepaticus strain ATCC 51449 [57]; three strains of H. pylori ([58]-[60]: 26695, J99 and HPAG1, respectively); Helicobacter acinonychis strain Sheeba [61]; and the deep-sea vent taxa Nitratiruptor sp. and Sulfurovum sp. (strains SB155-2 and NBC37-1, respectively [62]). This study presents the genomic sequence of a human clinical isolate, A. butzleri strain RM4018, a derivative of the type strain ATCC 49616. The genomic data revealed multiple differences between A. butzleri and other members of the Campylobacteraceae, as well as pathways and systems vital for its survival in diverse environments.
###end p 13

###begin p 16
###xml 14 33 14 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 184 194 184 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurovum</italic>
###xml 261 277 261 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. denitrificans</italic>
###xml 315 330 315 330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 494 501 494 501 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 570 579 570 579 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 14 47 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018</span>
###xml 261 277 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">S. denitrificans</span>
###xml 315 330 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
The genome of Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018 contains 2,341,251 bp; as such it is the second largest characterized epsilonproteobacterial genome to date, smaller than the genome of Sulfurovum strain NBC37-1 (2,562,277 bp) but larger than both the genomes of S. denitrificans strain ATCC 33889 (2,201,561 bp) and W. succinogenes strain DSM 1740 (2,110,355 bp). The G+C content of the RM4018 genome (27%) is remarkably low. A summary of the features of the strain RM4018 genome is provided in Table 1. A diagrammatic representation of the RM4018 genome is presented in Figure S1.
###end p 16
###begin title 17
###xml 16 35 16 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 16 42 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">Arcobacter butzleri RM4018</span>
Features of the Arcobacter butzleri RM4018 genome
###end title 17
###begin p 18
Total does not include pseudogenes.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 4 8 4 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hsdM</italic>
###xml 27 31 27 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hsdS</italic>
###xml 32 36 32 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hsdM</italic>
###xml 99 103 99 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hsdR</italic>
One hsdM pseudogene and an hsdS/hsdM pair are present but no complete Type I R/M system (including hsdR) is present.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 502 509 502 509 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 654 662 654 662 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s003">Table S1</xref>
###xml 730 738 730 738 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s004">Table S2</xref>
Consistent with its size, the RM4018 genome is predicted to encode 2259 coding sequences (CDSs). Based on pairwise BLASTP comparisons of proteins predicted to be encoded by these CDSs against proteins in the NCBI non-redundant (nr) database (release 10/13/2007), and on the presence of various Pfam and PROSITE motifs, 1011 (45%) of the predicted proteins were assigned a specific function, 505 (22%) were attributed only a general function, and 743 (33%) were considered proteins of unknown function (Table 1). A complete list of the CDSs predicted to be present within the genome of strain RM4018 and their annotation is presented in the supplementary Table S1. A breakdown of the CDSs by function is presented in supplementary Table S2.
###end p 20
###begin title 21
###xml 16 27 16 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 16 27 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Relationship of A. butzleri to other taxa
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 46 64 46 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 96 109 96 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 114 130 114 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurospirillum</italic>
###xml 179 189 179 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 194 207 194 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 315 331 315 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. denitrificans</italic>
###xml 336 351 336 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 387 404 387 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 406 413 406 413 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 512 522 512 522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurovum</italic>
###xml 526 539 526 539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>
###xml 630 634 630 634 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Nakagawa1">[62]</xref>
###xml 653 669 653 669 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. denitrificans</italic>
###xml 741 759 741 759 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 926 942 926 942 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. denitrificans</italic>
###xml 988 995 988 995 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 1024 1032 1024 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. fetus</italic>
###xml 1071 1082 1071 1082 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1215 1226 1215 1226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1232 1240 1232 1240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. fetus</italic>
###xml 0 19 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
###xml 315 331 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">S. denitrificans</span>
###xml 336 351 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 653 669 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">S. denitrificans</span>
###xml 926 942 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">S. denitrificans</span>
###xml 1024 1032 <span type="species:ncbi:196">C. fetus</span>
###xml 1071 1082 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1215 1226 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1232 1240 <span type="species:ncbi:196">C. fetus</span>
Arcobacter butzleri is a member of the family Campylobacteraceae which includes also the genera Campylobacter and Sulfurospirillum. Given the close taxonomic relationship between Arcobacter and Campylobacter, it is noteworthy that 17.2% and 12.4% of the RM4018 proteins have their best match in proteins encoded by S. denitrificans and W. succinogenes, respectively, both members of the Helicobacteraceae (Table 2). Moreover, approximately 25% of the RM4018 proteins have their best match in proteins encoded by Sulfurovum or Nitratiruptor, deep-sea vent Epsilonproteobacteria isolated from a sulfide mound off the coast of Japan [62].The percentage of S. denitrificans homologs with best matches is greater than that of the eight sequenced Campylobacteraceae species combined (13.1%). These differences are reduced somewhat by comparing the top five matches and not just the best match; however, even using these parameters, S. denitrificans (9.6%) remains the closest related organism (Table 2). Among the Campylobacters, C. fetus (3.1% best matches) is the closest to A. butzleri, although it is possible that other Campylobacters, whose genomes are as yet un-sequenced, may have higher degrees of similarity to A. butzleri than C. fetus.
###end p 22
###begin title 23
###xml 24 35 24 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 24 35 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Similarity of predicted A. butzleri proteins to proteins from other taxa.
###end title 23
###begin p 24
###xml 29 37 29 37 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s005">Table S3</xref>
###xml 49 68 49 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 179 180 179 180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 196 198 196 198 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;5</sup>
###xml 382 390 382 390 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s005">Table S3</xref>
###xml 49 68 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
Top matches are derived from Table S3. Predicted Arcobacter butzleri proteins were compared to proteins in the NCBI non-redundant (nr) database by BLASTP. Matches with an Expect (E) value of >1x10-5, an identity of <25%, and an alignment length across either the query or match sequences of <75% were excluded. The top five matches (where applicable) were identified at each locus (Table S3) and classified by taxon. Individual orders are listed if they constitute >1% of the total.
###end p 24
###begin p 25
A total of 1944 loci contained matches to proteins in the nr database, according to the criteria listed above. Percentage values for the defined taxa do not include the 315 loci (13.9% of the 2259 identified loci) for which no homologs were identified.
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 43 52 43 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 64 73 64 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 43 59 <span type="species:ncbi:195099">C. jejuni RM1221</span>
###xml 64 73 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>

###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 14 25 14 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 340 347 340 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 368 380 368 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Marinobacter</italic>
###xml 382 397 382 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Alteromonadales</italic>
###xml 400 415 400 415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Oceanospirillum</italic>
###xml 417 434 417 434 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Oceanospirillales</italic>
###xml 440 451 440 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>
###xml 453 468 453 468 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonadales</italic>
###xml 563 576 563 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clostridiales</italic>
###xml 742 743 742 743 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 758 760 758 760 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;5</sup>
###xml 827 835 827 835 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 837 844 837 844 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 846 854 846 854 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s005">Table S3</xref>
###xml 14 25 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
In the entire A. butzleri strain RM4018 proteome (unique and non-unique), 61.5% (1390/2259) of the proteins have their best matches in proteins encoded by the epsilonproteobacterial taxa, and 79.0% (1785/2259) are similar to Proteobacterial proteins. Most of the matches to non-Epsilonproteobacteria are found within the gamma subdivision (Table 2), in genera such as Marinobacter (Alteromonadales), Oceanospirillum (Oceanospirillales) and Pseudomonas (Pseudomonadales). Other phyla with a moderate number of protein matches include Firmicutes (2.5%), especially Clostridiales (1.5%), and Bacteroidetes/Chlorobi (2.8%). Among the 2259 predicted CDSs of strain RM4018, 315 (13.9%) had no homolog within the nr database using a minimum expect (E) value of 1x10-5, a minimum identity of 25% and a minimum alignment length of 75% (Figure 1, Table 2, Table S3).
###end p 27
###begin title 28
###xml 26 37 26 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 26 37 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Genome BLAST atlas of the A. butzleri strain RM4018.
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 147 160 147 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 190 202 190 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 342 347 342 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-5">[147]</xref>
###xml 0 33 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018</span>
Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018 is the reference genome and is compared to a set of 15 other epsilonproteobacterial genomes, including different Campylobacter (rings 7-14 from center) and Helicobacter (rings 15-17 from center) strains, as well as the UniProt database (outermost ring in black). A web-based "zoomable atlas" can be found at [147].
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 34 45 34 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 339 347 339 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s004">Table S2</xref>
###xml 349 357 349 357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s005">Table S3</xref>
###xml 854 864 854 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 34 52 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">A. butzleri RM4018</span>
Although approximately 30% of the A. butzleri RM4018 proteins with homologs within the nr database have their best matches to non-epsilonproteobacterial proteins, the approximately 550 genes encoding these proteins are not distributed randomly through the RM4018 genome, but rather clustered with respect to position and protein function (Table S2, Table S3). Interestingly, many of these clusters contain proteins involved in transport, and several contain discrete loci associated with a single function, such as the urease and quinohemoprotein loci described below. The genes contained in these loci are found often in the same order as in other taxa, suggesting lateral transfer. However, the G+C content of these gene clusters is not significantly different from the genome as a whole, suggesting that if these clusters were acquired from other non-Arcobacter taxa the acquisition was not recent.
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 217 224 217 224 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 602 620 600 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 635 642 633 640 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 872 879 866 873 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t003">Table 3</xref>
Generally, strain RM4018 proteins involved in "housekeeping" functions (e.g. amino acid biosynthesis, fatty acid biosynthesis and protein synthesis) have homologs well-conserved among the other Epsilonproteobacteria (Table 3). Nevertheless, a number of other major functional categories are more divergent. For example, 19% (13/70) of the strain RM4018 proteins involved in DNA replication and repair have either no homologs or homologs of low similarity (</= 35% identity) among the other epsilonproteobacterial taxa; this proportion increases to 37% (26/70) if proteins with homologs only within the Campylobacteraceae are included (Table 3). Other divergent functional categories include: sulfur/nitrogen metabolism (34%), transcriptional regulators/sigma-factors (47%), signal transduction (49%), cell envelope (37%), chemotaxis (70%) and antibiotic resistance (36%) (Table 3). These divergent functional categories will be discussed in further detail.
###end p 31
