###begin title 38
Methyl-directed mismatch repair and the absence of polynucleotide G:C tracts
###end title 38
###begin p 39
###xml 373 377 369 373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Iyer1">[63]</xref>
###xml 383 394 379 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 679 683 675 679 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Malik1">[64]</xref>
###xml 695 706 691 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 809 820 805 816 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1106 1117 1102 1113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1435 1442 1427 1434 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1447 1448 1439 1440 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1455 1456 1447 1448 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1464 1468 1456 1460 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Viswanathan1">[65]</xref>
###xml 1646 1659 1638 1651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 1664 1676 1656 1668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 1731 1742 1723 1734 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1813 1829 1805 1821 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. denitrificans</italic>
###xml 1834 1849 1826 1841 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 2011 2015 2001 2005 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Viswanathan2">[66]</xref>
###xml 2182 2193 2170 2181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 2244 2257 2232 2245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 2262 2274 2250 2262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 383 401 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">A. butzleri RM4018</span>
###xml 695 706 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 809 820 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1106 1117 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1435 1442 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1731 1749 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">A. butzleri RM4018</span>
###xml 1813 1829 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">S. denitrificans</span>
###xml 1834 1849 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 2182 2193 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Members of the Epsilonproteobacteria lack multiple genes in the methyl-directed mismatch repair system (MMR). The MMR system depends upon the presence of three main functions: 1) the MutSLH endonuclease complex, 2) a methylation system to identify parental vs. daughter strands and 3) multiple 5'-->3' and 3'-->5' single-strand DNA exonucleases, e.g. RecJ, ExoI and ExoVII [63]. The A. butzleri RM4018 genome is not predicted to encode MutL or MutH. However, it is predicted to encode a MutS2 family MutS protein, which is distinguished from MutS1 by the presence of a C-terminal Smr domain. It has been proposed that the Smr domain has a MutH-like nicking endonuclease function [64]. Thus, the A. butzleri MutS2 protein may contain both MutS and MutH domains, obviating the need for a MutL scaffold protein. A. butzleri strain RM4018 is not predicted to encode a Dam DNA-adenine methyltransferase (data not shown) used commonly in MMR systems, but the presence of a Dcm DNA-cytosine methyltransferase was demonstrated experimentally in strain RM4018 (data not shown); this Dcm function may be used by the A. butzleri MMR system to distinguish between parental and daughter strands. Although the annotated epsilonproteobacterial genomes contain the 5'-->3' exonuclease RecJ, they do not contain the 3'-->5' exonucleases ExoI or ExoVII. A 32-fold increase in +1 frameshifts and an 11-fold increase in -1 frameshifts were observed in an E. coli ExoI- ExoVII- mutant [65]; therefore, one possible outcome of such a defect in MMR systems would be the formation and extension of hypervariable G:C tracts, such as those identified in all characterized Campylobacter and Helicobacter genomes. A major distinguishing characteristic of the A. butzleri RM4018 genome is the lack of such G:C tracts, a feature shared by the S. denitrificans and W. succinogenes genomes. A comparison of these three genomes revealed the presence of two to four members of the DnaQ superfamily, to which the 3'-->5' exonuclease ExoX belongs [66]. Thus, one or more of these DnaQ homologs may provide the missing 3'-->5' exonuclease function, and it is conceivable that the absence of hypervariable G:C tracts in A. butzleri strain RM4018 and the presence of these tracts in Campylobacter and Helicobacter may be due to the presence or absence of a functional MMR system, respectively.
###end p 39
###begin title 40
Sulfur assimilation, oxidation and the biosynthesis of sulfur-containing amino acids
###end title 40
###begin p 41
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 106 114 106 114 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 421 428 421 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. coli</italic>
###xml 503 507 503 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cysC</italic>
###xml 566 570 566 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cysQ</italic>
###xml 629 636 629 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. coli</italic>
###xml 0 33 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018</span>
###xml 421 428 <span type="species:ncbi:195">C. coli</span>
###xml 629 636 <span type="species:ncbi:195">C. coli</span>
Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018 contains a number of genes required for sulfur uptake and assimilation (Figure 2). These genes include those encoding the sulfate ABC transporter CysATW, the sulfate binding protein Sbp, the ATP sulfhydrylase CysDN, the adenosine phosphosulfate (APS) reductase CysH, the sulfite reductase proteins CysI and CysJ and the siroheme synthase CysG. CysD and CysN have been identified also in C. coli, but the position of these genes, along with the APS kinase-encoding gene cysC and the 3'(2'),5'-bisphosphate nucleotidase-encoding gene cysQ, is in the capsular locus, suggesting that these genes in C. coli are involved in the formation or modification of the capsule and not sulfur assimilation per se.
###end p 41
###begin title 42
Sulfur assimilation and biosynthesis of the sulfur-containing amino acids.
###end title 42
###begin p 43
###xml 46 64 46 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 82 100 82 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
Genes/proteins in strain RM4018 unique within Campylobacteraceae or proteins with Campylobacteraceae orthologs of low similarity are labeled/shaded in blue.
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 155 159 155 159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Kredich1">[67]</xref>
###xml 320 324 320 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Kredich1">[67]</xref>
###xml 413 417 413 417 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Neuwald1">[68]</xref>
###xml 419 423 419 423 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Valdes1">[69]</xref>
###xml 510 523 510 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 523 527 523 527 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Bick1">[70]</xref>
###xml 532 547 532 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M. tuberculosis</italic>
###xml 547 551 547 551 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Williams1">[71]</xref>
###xml 727 731 727 731 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Bick1">[70]</xref>
###xml 733 737 733 737 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Williams1">[71]</xref>
###xml 510 523 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 532 547 <span type="species:ncbi:1773">M. tuberculosis</span>
Intracellular sulfate is reduced to sulfite in bacteria by one of two pathways. Both pathways first convert sulfate to APS via the ATP sulfhydrylase CysDN [67]. The first pathway converts APS to PAPS (phosphoadenosine phosphosulfate) using the kinase CysC, and then reduces PAPS to sulfite using the PAPS reductase CysH [67]; PAPS toxicity in some taxa is decreased through the conversion of PAPS to APS via CysQ [68], [69]. The second pathway, identified originally in plants and subsequently in taxa such as P. aeruginosa[70] and M. tuberculosis[71], reduces APS to sulfite directly using the APS reductase CysH. The presence of conserved two-cysteine motifs in strain RM4018 CysH, characteristic of bacterial APS reductases [70], [71], and the absence of both CysC and CysQ homologs, suggests that sulfate reduction to sulfite in this strain does not use a PAPS intermediate.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 175 183 175 183 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 239 240 239 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 276 279 276 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 287 293 287 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0563</italic>
###xml 294 300 294 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0570</italic>
###xml 636 639 636 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 695 718 695 718 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Paracoccus pantotrophus</italic>
###xml 718 722 718 722 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Friedrich1">[72]</xref>
###xml 724 728 724 728 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Wodara1">[73]</xref>
###xml 730 748 730 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Chlorobium tepidum</italic>
###xml 748 752 748 752 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Eisen1">[74]</xref>
###xml 757 781 757 781 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rhodovulum sulfidophilum</italic>
###xml 781 785 781 785 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-AppiaAyme1">[75]</xref>
###xml 872 882 872 882 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">soxXYZABCD</italic>
###xml 919 923 919 923 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Friedrich2">[76]</xref>
###xml 983 984 983 984 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 1140 1144 1140 1144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Friedrich2">[76]</xref>
###xml 1342 1346 1342 1346 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Friedrich2">[76]</xref>
###xml 1463 1466 1463 1466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 1515 1519 1515 1519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">soxV</italic>
###xml 1519 1523 1519 1523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-AppiaAyme2">[77]</xref>
###xml 1525 1529 1525 1529 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Bagchi1">[78]</xref>
###xml 1774 1784 1774 1784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurovum</italic>
###xml 1786 1799 1786 1799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>
###xml 1804 1820 1804 1820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. denitrificans</italic>
###xml 1822 1830 1822 1830 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s004">Table S2</xref>
###xml 1972 1975 1972 1975 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 2067 2070 2067 2070 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 2105 2109 2105 2109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">soxY</italic>
###xml 2114 2118 2114 2118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">soxZ</italic>
###xml 2228 2238 2228 2238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurovum</italic>
###xml 2240 2253 2240 2253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>
###xml 2258 2275 2258 2275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. denitrificans.</italic>
###xml 2280 2283 2280 2283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 2343 2354 2343 2354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 2398 2401 2398 2401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 2464 2477 2464 2477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. halophilus</italic>
###xml 2554 2557 2554 2557 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sox</italic>
###xml 2609 2619 2609 2619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 2671 2681 2671 2681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 2693 2703 2693 2703 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sulfurovum</italic>
###xml 695 718 <span type="species:ncbi:82367">Paracoccus pantotrophus</span>
###xml 730 748 <span type="species:ncbi:1097">Chlorobium tepidum</span>
###xml 757 781 <span type="species:ncbi:35806">Rhodovulum sulfidophilum</span>
###xml 1804 1820 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">S. denitrificans</span>
###xml 2258 2274 <span type="species:ncbi:39766">S. denitrificans</span>
###xml 2343 2354 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 2464 2477 <span type="species:ncbi:197482">A. halophilus</span>
The sulfite generated by strain RM4018 CysH has two potential fates: reduction to sulfide and assimilation into the sulfur-containing amino acids L-cysteine and L-methionine (Figure 2), or oxidation to sulfate, facilitated by a cytochrome c multienzyme complex encoded by the sox genes (ab0563-ab0570). Initial data indicated that sulfite is oxidized by strain RM4018 (data not shown), and also that it can grow in minimal media without added cysteine or methionine (data not shown). Hence, both metabolic fates are possible, and the genetic switch modulating oxidation or reduction of sulfite remains to be identified. Homologs of the sox genes have been identified in multiple taxa, including Paracoccus pantotrophus[72], [73], Chlorobium tepidum[74] and Rhodovulum sulfidophilum[75]. The Sox clusters of some organisms can contain as many as 15 genes, but seven genes (soxXYZABCD) are essential for sulfur oxidation [76]. These seven genes encode four proteins: the heterodimeric c-type cytochrome SoxXA, the heterodimeric sulfur-binding protein SoxYZ, the heterotetrameric SoxCD sulfur dehydrogenase and the thiol sulfate esterase SoxB [76]. Sulfite, sulfide, sulfur and thiosulfate are possible substrates for the Sox complex; thiosulfate and sulfide oxidation requires the entire complex, while sulfite oxidation does not require SoxCD [76]. The presence of SoxCD in strain RM4018 would suggest that thiosulfate is oxidized by this organism. However, other sox genes important for thiosulfate oxidation, e.g. soxV[77], [78], are absent in this strain, as well as the Sbp-related thiosulfate-binding protein CysP. Thus, it is possible that only sulfite and sulfide are oxidized in strain RM4018. Sox proteins are present also in the related epsilonproteobacterial taxa Sulfurovum, Nitratiruptor and S. denitrificans (Table S2). However, there are multiple differences between the sulfur oxidation systems of these related organisms and those of strain RM4018: 1) the sox genes in strain RM4018 form a single cluster instead of two clusters, 2) the strain RM4018 sox cluster contains only one copy of soxY and soxZ and 3) no significant similarity exists between the SoxXA protein of strain RM4018 and the SoxXA proteins of Sulfurovum, Nitratiruptor and S. denitrificans. The sox cluster of strain RM4018 was not detected in 12 additional A. butzleri strains (see below). However, a cluster of sox genes similar to that of strain RM4018 has been identified in A. halophilus (data not shown). Thus, it appears that strain RM4018 may have acquired the sox cluster through lateral gene transfer from another Arcobacter species and that the sulfur oxidation machinery of Arcobacter and, e.g., Sulfurovum are likely to be distinct evolutionarily.
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 139 147 139 147 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 391 395 391 395 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Kredich1">[67]</xref>
The genome of strain RM4018 contains all of the genes necessary for the biosynthesis of L-cysteine, L-methionine and iron-sulfur clusters (Figure 2). Consistent with the proposed absence of thiosulfate metabolism, the bacterium has only a gene encoding the CysK cysteine synthase A and not the CysM cysteine synthase B that utilizes thiosulfate instead of sulfide to produce S-sulfocysteine [67]. Strain RM4018 also contains both the cobalamin-dependent and cobalamin-independent homocysteine transmethylases MetH and MetE.
###end p 46
###begin title 47
###xml 26 37 26 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 26 37 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
The central metabolism of A. butzleri
###end title 47
###begin p 48
###xml 184 203 184 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 305 313 305 313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 472 483 472 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 184 217 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018</span>
###xml 472 483 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
The general function of the citric acid/tricarboxylic acid (TCA) cycle is to oxidize organic tri- and di-carboxylic acids to provide energy and biosynthetic precursors for metabolism. Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018 encodes several proteins homologous to other epsilonproteobacterial TCA cycle enzymes (Figure 3), e.g. isocitrate dehydrogenase (AB1321), 2-oxoglutarate dehydrogenase (AB0852-AB0855), malate dehydrogenase (AB1322) and citrate synthase (AB0307). However, A. butzleri strain RM4018 is predicted putatively to encode two aconitate hydratases and two fumarate dehydratases. Additionally, enzymes that catalyze two TCA cycle steps are absent apparently in strain RM4018.
###end p 48
###begin title 49
###xml 55 66 55 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 55 66 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Predicted TCA, methylcitrate and citramalate cycles of A. butzleri strain RM4018.
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 24 42 24 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
Genes unique within the Campylobacteraceae are labeled in green. Genes in parentheses encode multi-subunit proteins or a protein and its cognate accessory protein. 1: pyruvate dehydrogenase; 2: L-lactate dehydrogenase; 3: phosphate transacetylase; 4: acetate kinase; 5: citrate synthase; 6: aconitase; 7: isocitrate dehydrogenase; 8: 2-oxoglutarate:acceptor oxidoreductase; 9: fumarate reductase; 10: fumarase; 11: malate dehydrogenase; 12: malate:quinone oxidoreductase; 13: 2-methylcitrate synthase; 14: 2-methylcitrate dehydratase; 15: aconitase; 16: 2-methylisocitrate lyase; 17: malic enzyme; 18: malyl-CoA hydrolase; 19: malyl-CoA lyase; 20: beta-methylmalyl-CoA lyase; 21: mesaconyl-CoA hydratase; 22: mesaconyl-CoA synthetase; 23: citramalate hydrolase; 24: citramalate lyase.
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 10 16 10 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0275</italic>
###xml 21 27 21 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1447</italic>
###xml 62 69 62 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 120 139 120 139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 227 246 227 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 264 270 264 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0275</italic>
###xml 438 464 438 464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Alkaliliminicola ehrlichei</italic>
###xml 496 503 496 503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 540 546 540 546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0275</italic>
###xml 820 824 820 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acnD</italic>
###xml 833 839 833 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0276</italic>
###xml 903 914 903 914 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 984 988 984 988 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Grimek1">[79]</xref>
###xml 62 69 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 120 139 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
###xml 227 246 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
###xml 496 503 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 903 914 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
The genes ab0275 and ab1447 encode proteins homologous to the E. coli aconitate hydratases AcnA and AcnB, respectively. Arcobacter butzleri AcnB shares between 62% and 76% identity with other epsilonproteobacterial aconitases. Arcobacter butzleri AcnD, encoded by ab0275, does not have significant similarity with any of the known epsilonproteobacterial proteins, but has an 82% similarity with the PrpD 2-methylisocitrate dehydratase of Alkaliliminicola ehrlichei as well as 68% similarity with E. coli AcnA. In addition, the proximity of ab0275 to genes that encode the methylcitrate pathway enzymes PrpB and PrpC suggests that in strain RM4018 AcnD is the aconitase of the methylcitrate pathway and AcnB is the aconitase of the TCA cycle. Also, the absence of the 2-methylcitrate dehydratase PrpD and the presence of acnD next to ab0276, which encodes the AcnD-associated protein PrpF, suggests that A. butzleri strain RM4018 contains the alternate AcnD/PrpF methylcitrate pathway [79].
###end p 51
###begin p 52
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 293 300 293 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 403 410 403 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 578 593 578 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 613 626 613 626 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H. hepaticus.</italic>
###xml 677 692 677 692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 729 741 729 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H. hepaticus</italic>
###xml 888 903 888 903 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 907 919 907 919 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H. hepaticus</italic>
###xml 950 962 950 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri.</italic>
###xml 0 16 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 293 300 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 403 410 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 578 593 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 613 625 <span type="species:ncbi:32025">H. hepaticus</span>
###xml 677 692 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 729 741 <span type="species:ncbi:32025">H. hepaticus</span>
###xml 888 903 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 907 919 <span type="species:ncbi:32025">H. hepaticus</span>
###xml 950 961 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Escherichia coli can express three fumarases: A, B and C. The first two contain iron-sulfur clusters and are unstable aerobically; fumarase C is stable in the presence of oxygen. The genome of strain RM4018 is predicted to encode two fumarases: AB0722 and AB1921. AB0722 has 74% similarity to E. coli fumarase C and would be predicted to be active under aerobic conditions. AB1921 has 48% similarity to E. coli fumarases A and B and would require microaerobic or anaerobic conditions. AB1921 also has 55-64% similarities with two proteins encoded by the obligate microaerophile W. succinogenes and two encoded by H. hepaticus. Interestingly, the sequence similarities with the W. succinogenes proteins WS1766 and WS1767, and the H. hepaticus proteins HH1702 and HH1793 correspond to the first 282 and the last 185 residues of AB1921, respectively, suggesting that the two polypeptides in W. succinogenes or H. hepaticus are fused into one protein in A. butzleri.
###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 119 130 119 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 160 173 160 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0296-ab0298</italic>
###xml 259 294 259 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni, H. hepaticus, H. pylori,</italic>
###xml 299 315 299 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes,</italic>
###xml 428 435 428 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 440 449 440 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 505 514 505 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H. pylori</italic>
###xml 519 534 519 534 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 884 895 884 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1190 1201 1190 1201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1210 1216 1210 1216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0296</italic>
###xml 1217 1223 1217 1223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0298</italic>
###xml 1250 1258 1250 1258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 119 130 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 259 268 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 270 282 <span type="species:ncbi:32025">H. hepaticus</span>
###xml 284 293 <span type="species:ncbi:210">H. pylori</span>
###xml 299 314 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 428 435 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 440 449 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 505 514 <span type="species:ncbi:210">H. pylori</span>
###xml 519 534 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 884 895 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1190 1201 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
No genes encoding the SucCD succinyl-CoA synthetase or the SdhABCD succinate dehydrogenase have been identified in the A. butzleri genome, but the gene cluster ab0296-ab0298 encodes proteins with high similarities (71-85%) to the fumarate reductase FrdABC of C. jejuni, H. hepaticus, H. pylori, and W. succinogenes, which catalyzes the reaction in the reductive direction converting fumarate to succinate. Some bacteria such as E. coli and C. jejuni have genes encoding both Sdh and Frd, and others, e.g. H. pylori and W. succinogenes, encode only Frd. The similar structures of Sdh and Frd preclude predicting, solely from sequence analyses, whether an enzyme is one or the other. Regulation of transcriptional levels by the oxygen content in the atmosphere permits differentiation between both enzymes; obligate aerobes encode Sdh and anaerobes encode Frd. Initial experiments with A. butzleri indicated the presence of fumarate reduction and no succinate oxidation, and this activity increased several-fold in bacteria grown under anaerobic conditions relative to bacteria grown under aerobic conditions (data not shown). These results provided evidence supporting the identification of A. butzleri FrdABC (ab0296-ab0298) as a fumarate reductase (Figure 3).
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 84 90 84 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1917</italic>
###xml 91 97 91 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1921</italic>
###xml 157 161 157 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Friedmann1">[80]</xref>
###xml 163 167 163 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Hallam1">[81]</xref>
###xml 194 198 194 198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Berg1">[82]</xref>
###xml 200 204 200 204 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Ivanovsky1">[83]</xref>
###xml 283 291 283 291 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 925 931 910 916 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1918</italic>
###xml 980 986 965 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1921</italic>
###xml 1267 1273 1252 1258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1069</italic>
###xml 1513 1521 1498 1506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g003">Figure 3</xref>
The genome of strain RM4018 may contain also a pathway, encoded by the gene cluster ab1917-ab1921, which resembles segments of the 3-hydroxypropionate cycle [80], [81] and the citramalate cycle [82], [83], and interconverts glyoxylate and propionyl-CoA with pyruvate and acetyl-CoA (Figure 3). AB1917 and AB1920 are similar to the CitE citrate lyase. In addition, AB1918 is an acetyl-CoA synthetase with a CaiC domain in residues 50-550, and a CitE domain in residues 550-825. CitE domains have strong similarity to malyl-CoA lyases and have lesser homology to malate synthetase domains. Thus, any of these three proteins could function as a malyl-CoA lyase. AB1919 has a approximately73% similarity to enol-CoA hydratase which catalyzes reversible reactions interconverting 2-enoyl-CoA compounds, such as mesaconyl-CoA, and 3-hydroxyacyl-CoA compounds, such as beta-methylmalate-CoA. If the acetyl-CoA synthetase encoded by ab1918 and the anaerobic fumarate hydratase encoded by ab1921 were broad specificity enzymes, the former could catalyze the synthesis of mesaconyl-CoA from mesaconate, and the latter the interconversion of mesaconate and citramalate. Finally, citramalate could be synthesized from pyruvate and acetyl-CoA by one of the CitE enzymes. The gene ab1069 encodes an acyl-CoA thioester hydrolase which can catalyze the synthesis of malyl-CoA from malate or the reverse reaction. One of the three citrate lyases mentioned could then convert malyl-CoA to glyoxylate and acetyl-CoA and glyoxylate (Figure 3).
###end p 54
###begin p 55
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 528 542 528 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1480-ab1482.</italic>
###xml 726 733 726 733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1083,</italic>
###xml 0 19 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
Arcobacter butzleri does not grow on acetate, citrate, propionate or acetate with propionate, and it grows on fumarate, lactate, malate and pyruvate (data not shown). These data suggested that the methylcitrate pathway would function to produce oxaloacetate for the TCA cycle and propionyl-CoA. The latter metabolite together with glyoxylate synthesized from malate via malyl-CoA would be converted to acetyl-CoA and pyruvate. Acetyl-CoA could be synthesized also from pyruvate via the pyruvate dehydrogenase complex encoded by ab1480-ab1482. Alternatively, the methylcitrate pathway could have a regulatory role converting any excess propionyl-CoA to succinate and pyruvate. Through the activity of a malic enzyme encoded by ab1083, pyruvate can be carboxylated to malate and used to replenish the TCA cycle.
###end p 55
###begin title 56
Anaerobic and aerobic respiration
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 0 11 0 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 155 156 155 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 189 191 189 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bd</italic>
###xml 212 213 212 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 223 226 223 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cbb</italic>
###xml 253 261 253 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 489 494 489 494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hupSL</italic>
###xml 544 552 544 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hydABCDF</italic>
###xml 557 564 557 564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hyaABCD</italic>
###xml 629 630 629 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</italic>
###xml 1152 1153 1152 1153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</italic>
###xml 1153 1154 1153 1154 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1173 1174 1173 1174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</italic>
###xml 1174 1175 1174 1175 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 0 11 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
A. butzleri has a full complement of genes for aerobic/microaerobic respiration including those encoding NADH:quinone oxidoreductase, ubiquinol cytochrome c oxidase, ferredoxin, cytochrome bd oxidase, cytochrome c oxidase (cbb3-type), and F1/F0 ATPase (Figure 4), but it also has limited ability for anaerobic respiration. Potential electron donors, in addition to NADH, are hydrogen, malate and formate. One large gene cluster encodes three FeNi hydrogenases with one uptake hydrogenase (hupSL) and two membrane associated proteins encoded by hydABCDF and hyaABCD, the latter two predicted to be anchored to the membrane by the b-type cytochromes HydC and HyaC, respectively. There are two formate dehydrogenases, one selenocysteine homolog and one cysteine homolog, suggesting that selenium may be important in their regulation. Also present is a malate:quinone oxidoreductase (Mqo) and a putative lactate dehydrogenase (AB0728), suggesting that lactate may be a potential electron donor. Electrons may be transferred also to the menaquinone pool through the Sox system described above, the number of electrons depending on the substrate oxidized, 2 e- for sulfite and 8 e- for sulfide.
###end p 57
###begin title 58
###xml 24 35 24 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 24 35 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Respiratory pathways in A. butzleri strain RM4018.
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 160 161 160 161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</italic>
###xml 167 168 167 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 229 247 229 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacteraceae</italic>
###xml 450 451 450 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 522 523 522 523 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 548 549 548 549 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
Transfer of electrons to the menaquinone (MQ) pool is represented by blue arrows; transfer of electrons from the menaquinone pool is represented by red arrows. b- and c-type cytochromes are shaded yellow. Genes unique within the Campylobacteraceae are labeled in green. NADH:Q OR: NADH:quinone oxidoreductase; M:Q OR: malate:quinone oxidoreductase; FormDH: formate dehydrogenase; LacDH: L-lactate dehydrogenase; SulfDH: sulfur dehydrogenase; Ubi cyt c OR: Ubiquinol cytochrome c oxidoreductase; TMAO RD: TMAO reductase; NO3RD: nitrate reductase; NO2RD: nitrite reductase; FumRD: fumarate reductase; QHAmDH: quinohemoprotein amine dehydrogenase; AldDH: aldehyde dehydrogenase; PX: peroxidase; CTQ: cysteine tryptophylquinone.
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 271 274 271 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nap</italic>
###xml 333 346 333 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 563 564 563 564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 597 603 597 603 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1150</italic>
###xml 613 619 613 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1151</italic>
###xml 642 646 642 646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bisC</italic>
###xml 790 794 790 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">torC</italic>
###xml 799 803 799 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">torA</italic>
###xml 836 840 836 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">torD</italic>
###xml 949 955 949 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1360</italic>
###xml 986 987 986 987 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</italic>
###xml 1021 1027 1021 1027 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1987</italic>
Fumarate, nitrate and nitrite are used by strain RM4018 as electron acceptors. Fumarate can be reduced to succinate by the fumarate reductase FrdABC. Nitrate can be reduced to ammonia via a periplasmic nitrate reductase NapAB and a pentaheme nitrite reductase NrfAH. The nap operon has the same gene number and order as that seen in Campylobacter species. It is possible also that trimethylamine-oxide (TMAO) and/or dimethylsulfoxide (DMSO) may serve as alternative electron acceptors. Analysis of the strain RM4018 genome indicates the presence of the pentaheme c-type cytochrome TorC encoded by ab1150. The CDS ab1151 has been annotated as bisC, but the BisC family includes also other anaerobic dehydrogenases, such as the TMAO and DMSO reductases TorA and DmsA, respectively. The genes torC and torA are co-transcribed usually with torD, but no TorD homolog was detected in the strain RM4018 genome. Other electron acceptors may be present: CDS ab1360 encodes a putative cytochrome b-type nitric oxide reductase, and ab1987 encodes a putative nitrite/nitric oxide reductase. Additional investigations will be necessary to determine the function of these putative electron acceptors.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 51 62 51 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 366 370 355 359 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Takagi1">[84]</xref>
###xml 464 475 449 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 599 603 584 588 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Vandenberghe1">[85]</xref>
###xml 703 706 688 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cbb</italic>
###xml 744 745 729 730 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 745 749 730 734 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Takagi2">[86]</xref>
###xml 786 790 771 775 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Adachi1">[87]</xref>
###xml 806 814 791 799 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 981 1005 966 990 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Paracoccus denitrificans</italic>
###xml 1091 1095 1076 1080 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Ono1">[88]</xref>
###xml 1600 1604 1581 1585 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Hacisalihoglu1">[89]</xref>
###xml 1763 1769 1744 1750 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0376</italic>
###xml 1774 1780 1755 1761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab2135</italic>
###xml 1857 1865 1838 1846 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 51 62 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 464 475 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 981 1005 <span type="species:ncbi:266">Paracoccus denitrificans</span>
In addition to the respiratory proteins described, A. butzleri strain RM4018 is predicted to encode a quinohemoprotein amine dehydrogenase (QHAmDH), the presence of which is novel in the epsilon subdivision. QHAmDH is a heterotrimeric (alphabetagamma) protein that deaminates oxidatively a variety of aliphatic and aromatic amines, e.g. n-butylamine and benzylamine [84], and is unusual in that the small (gamma) subunit contains an intrinsic quinone cofactor [in A. butzleri, cysteine tryptophylquinone (CTQ)], formed by the covalent linkage of a cysteine residue to an oxidized tryptophan residue [85]. The presence of this intrinsic quinone cofactor permits the transfer of electrons directly to the cbb3 oxidase through either a cytochrome c[86] or blue-copper protein (e.g. azurin [87]) intermediate (Figure 4). The QHAmDH locus of strain RM4018 encodes also a radical SAM (S-Ado-Met) family protein (AB0466). A radical SAM protein (ORF2) is found also in the QHAmDH locus of Paracoccus denitrificans and has been proposed to play an important role in the formation of the CTQ cofactor [88]. Amino acid motifs conserved in ORF2 are 100% identical to those in AB0466, as well as to the relevant amino acids in the gamma subunit AB0467, suggesting that the strain RM4018 QHAmDH locus encodes a functional dehydrogenase. M9 minimal media amended with 0.5% n-butylamine-HCl (v/v), benzylamine-HCl (w/v) or methylamine-HCl (w/v) as a sole carbon source does not support the growth of strain RM4018 (data not shown). However, substrate specificity has been demonstrated among the amine-utilizing taxa [89]; therefore, it is likely that RM4018 utilizes an as yet unidentified aliphatic or aromatic amine. Finally, two aldehyde dehydrogenases, encoded putatively by ab0376 and ab2135, also novel in the Epsilonproteobacteria, were identified in strain RM4018 (Figure 4). Thus, it is possible that the aldehydes generated from the QHAmDH are oxidized further.
###end p 61
###begin title 62
Urease
###end title 62
###begin p 63
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 54 67 54 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0808-ab0813</italic>
###xml 441 445 430 434 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Goldie1">[90]</xref>
###xml 549 556 538 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. lari</italic>
###xml 565 577 554 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 685 697 667 679 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 771 783 753 765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 793 800 775 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. lari</italic>
###xml 845 857 827 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ureD(AB)CEFG</italic>
###xml 910 920 892 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Klebsiella</italic>
###xml 922 929 904 911 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Proteus</italic>
###xml 931 938 913 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 951 958 933 940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vibrio,</italic>
###xml 971 983 953 965 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 990 1002 972 984 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ure(AB)IEFGH</italic>
###xml 1064 1076 1046 1058 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 1175 1198 1157 1180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bacillus, Lactobacillus</italic>
###xml 1203 1215 1185 1197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Psychromonas</italic>
###xml 1217 1225 1199 1207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s005">Table S3</xref>
###xml 1362 1374 1344 1356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 1378 1385 1360 1367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. lari</italic>
###xml 1400 1412 1382 1394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 1459 1479 1441 1461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H. hepaticus nikABDE</italic>
###xml 1483 1497 1465 1479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H. pylori nixA</italic>
###xml 1694 1705 1676 1687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 0 33 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018</span>
###xml 549 556 <span type="species:ncbi:201">C. lari</span>
###xml 793 800 <span type="species:ncbi:201">C. lari</span>
###xml 931 946 <span type="species:ncbi:83334">E. coli O157:H7</span>
###xml 1378 1385 <span type="species:ncbi:201">C. lari</span>
###xml 1459 1471 <span type="species:ncbi:32025">H. hepaticus</span>
###xml 1483 1492 <span type="species:ncbi:210">H. pylori</span>
###xml 1694 1705 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018 contains six genes (ab0808-ab0813) involved in the degradation of urea. In bacteria this catabolism involves generally three sets of genes: a nickel-containing urease (composed of alpha, beta and gamma subunits), urease accessory proteins which deliver the nickel to the urease and a nickel uptake system. The urease of strain RM4018 is functional (data not shown), as determined by a phenol red/urea assay [90], although the level of activity is not as high as that found in other urease-producing taxa (e.g. UPTC C. lari). As in Helicobacter, the urease alpha and beta subunits are fused, and the strain RM4018 urease subunits show high homology to Helicobacter urease subunits. However, differences exist with the urease loci of both Helicobacter and UPTC C. lari. First, the gene order of the locus itself, ureD(AB)CEFG, is similar to the gene order of the urease loci in Klebsiella, Proteus, E. coli O157:H7 and Vibrio, but not the Helicobacter locus ure(AB)IEFGH. Second, although the urease enzyme itself is similar to the Helicobacter urease, the accessory proteins UreD, UreE and UreF, had greater similarity to those identified in Bacillus, Lactobacillus and Psychromonas (Table S3); additionally, the nickel-binding protein UreE has a histidine-rich C terminus, found in multiple UreE proteins, but not in those from Helicobacter or C. lari. Also, unlike Helicobacter, no obvious nickel uptake system, such as the H. hepaticus nikABDE or H. pylori nixA, was found in strain RM4018. A putative nickel transporter, AB1752, was identified, but it is unclear whether it is specific for nickel, or is a heavy-metal-ion transporter. Finally, although the A. butzleri urease may serve to degrade exogenous urea, it may also degrade endogenous urea, formed during putrescine biosynthesis, specifically during the conversion of agmatine to putrescine by SpeB (AB1578).
###end p 63
###begin title 64
Surface structures
###end title 64
###begin p 65
###xml 33 44 33 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 161 172 161 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 428 434 428 434 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1805</italic>
###xml 435 441 435 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1833</italic>
###xml 485 498 485 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 498 502 498 502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Parkhill1">[51]</xref>
###xml 504 508 504 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Fouts1">[52]</xref>
###xml 510 514 510 514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Gilbert1">[91]</xref>
###xml 516 520 516 520 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Parker1">[92]</xref>
###xml 562 574 562 574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 579 588 579 588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wolinella</italic>
###xml 764 772 764 772 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s004">Table S2</xref>
###xml 1011 1019 1011 1019 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s005">Table S3</xref>
###xml 1087 1098 1087 1098 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1202 1213 1202 1213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1219 1228 1219 1228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 1307 1311 1307 1311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Parker2">[93]</xref>
###xml 1353 1364 1353 1364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1469 1488 1469 1488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Salmonella enterica</italic>
###xml 1498 1502 1498 1502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Kaniuk1">[94]</xref>
###xml 33 44 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 161 172 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1087 1098 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1202 1213 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1219 1228 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 1353 1364 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1469 1488 <span type="species:ncbi:28901">Salmonella enterica</span>
SDS-PAGE analysis suggested that A. butzleri strain RM4018 can express lipooligosaccharide (LOS). To date, little is known about the roles of these molecules in A. butzleri. They generate great attention in bacterial pathogens since LOS/lipopolysaccharide (LPS) are major inducers of proinflammatory responses, are immunodominant antigens, and play a role in host cell interactions. The LOS biosynthesis locus of strain RM4018 (ab1805-ab1833) showed a similar organization to those of Campylobacter[51], [52], [91], [92], and is thus dissimilar from the loci of Helicobacter and Wolinella. At both ends of the locus are genes involved in the addition of heptose to the oligosaccharides and the encoded proteins are similar to those of other Epsilonproteobacteria (Table S2). Within the locus, genes are found whose products have functions related to LOS/LPS biosynthesis, including several glycosyltransferases, but the proteins encoded have greater similarity to proteins outside of the Epsilonproteobacteria (Table S3). This LOS/LPS biosynthesis region is conserved among 12 unrelated A. butzleri strains, based on comparative genomic indexing (described in detail later), which likely distinguishes A. butzleri from C. jejuni, where the LOS biosynthesis region is an intraspecies hypervariability region [93]. The gene conservation of this region in A. butzleri resembles more closely the conservation of the LPS core biosynthesis region occurring among many of the Salmonella enterica serovars [94].
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 152 163 152 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 222 228 222 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0661</italic>
###xml 229 235 229 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0697</italic>
###xml 321 325 321 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wbpG</italic>
###xml 327 331 327 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hisH</italic>
###xml 337 341 337 341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hisF</italic>
###xml 361 383 361 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 407 411 407 411 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Burrows1">[95]</xref>
###xml 540 548 540 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s004">Table S2</xref>
###xml 649 652 649 652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">kps</italic>
###xml 753 764 753 764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 896 907 896 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 979 990 979 990 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1111 1122 1111 1122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 152 163 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 361 383 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
###xml 753 764 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 896 907 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 979 990 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1111 1122 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Many bacteria synthesize structurally diverse polysaccharide polymers, O-antigen and capsule that are major antigenic determinants. It is possible that A. butzleri strain RM4018 produces O-antigen, since there is a locus (ab0661-ab0697) that encodes several additional glycosyltransferases. This region has two copies of wbpG, hisH, and hisF, found also in the Pseudomonas aeruginosa B-band O-antigen locus [95], and many of the other encoded proteins have greater similarity to proteins from bacteria outside of the Epsilonproteobacteria (Table S2). Although this region could be involved putatively in capsular formation, the absence of conserved kps capsular genes in this region, combined with the presence of O-antigen-related genes, suggests that A. butzleri strain RM4018 produces O-antigen and not capsule; however, further investigations will be necessary to determine the nature of the A. butzleri cell-surface structures. Like many O-antigen biosynthesis regions, the A. butzleri region appears to represent an intraspecies hypervariability region with the RM4018 region, present in only 1 of the 12 A. butzleri strains examined using comparative genomic indexing.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 378 391 378 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 396 408 396 408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 410 419 410 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 513 539 513 539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter/Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 690 710 690 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter jejuni</italic>
###xml 712 721 712 721 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0001358-g005">Figure 5B</xref>
###xml 790 796 790 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1931</italic>
###xml 797 803 797 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1961</italic>
###xml 861 867 861 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0197</italic>
###xml 868 874 868 874 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0208</italic>
###xml 887 893 887 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab2238</italic>
###xml 894 900 894 900 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab2244</italic>
###xml 953 966 953 966 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>
###xml 1083 1096 1083 1096 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>
###xml 1179 1190 1179 1190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1195 1221 1195 1221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter/Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 1266 1279 1266 1279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nitratiruptor</italic>
###xml 1365 1369 1365 1369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Nakagawa1">[62]</xref>
###xml 0 33 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018</span>
###xml 690 710 <span type="species:ncbi:197">Campylobacter jejuni</span>
###xml 1179 1190 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018 is a motile bacterium that synthesizes a polar flagellum. Many of the flagellar apparatus proteins encoded by strain RM4018 have homologs in other epsilonproteobacterial taxa. However, phylogenetic analysis of selected flagellar proteins suggests that the flagellar apparatus of strain RM4018 has an evolutionary history distinct from those of Campylobacter and Helicobacter (Figure 5A). This distinct history is supported also by predicted differences between strain RM4018 and Campylobacter/Helicobacter in flagellar gene regulation (see below). Additionally, the flagellar genes of strain RM4018 are highly clustered, compared to the flagellar genes of Campylobacter jejuni (Figure 5B). The primary cluster in strain RM4018 contains 20 flagellar genes (ab1931-ab1961) with the other two flagellar clusters containing eight (ab0197-ab0208) and three (ab2238-ab2244) genes. The flagellar genes of the related organism Nitratiruptor are also highly clustered with the primary cluster containing 36 flagellar and chemotaxis genes. Significantly, the Nitratiruptor flagellar proteins also appear to be distinct phylogenetically from those of both A. butzleri and Campylobacter/Helicobacter. Moreover, the primary flagellar cluster of Nitratiruptor has an atypical G+C content, suggesting acquisition through horizontal gene transfer [62]. Although the G+C content of the strain RM4018 flagellar genes is not atypical, it is possible that the flagellar genes of this organism were acquired via a similar mechanism.
###end p 67
