###begin title 70
Prophage and genomic islands
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 18 29 18 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 145 151 145 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1655</italic>
###xml 152 158 152 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1706</italic>
###xml 599 630 599 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli, Neisseria meningitidis</italic>
###xml 632 655 632 655 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Deinococcus radiodurans</italic>
###xml 657 679 657 679 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Haemophilus influenzae</italic>
###xml 681 705 681 705 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Burkholderia cenocepacia</italic>
###xml 705 709 705 709 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Morgan1">[96]</xref>
###xml 711 715 711 715 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Summer1">[97]</xref>
###xml 728 737 728 737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 759 763 759 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Fouts1">[52]</xref>
###xml 765 769 765 769 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Parker2">[93]</xref>
###xml 872 880 872 880 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s004">Table S2</xref>
###xml 939 940 939 940 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</underline>
###xml 950 951 950 951 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</underline>
###xml 953 954 953 954 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">l</underline>
###xml 958 959 958 959 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</underline>
###xml 1057 1070 1057 1070 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 1085 1095 1085 1095 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 1113 1131 1113 1131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter bilis</italic>
###xml 1133 1137 1133 1137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Parker2">[93]</xref>
###xml 18 29 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 599 606 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 608 630 <span type="species:ncbi:487">Neisseria meningitidis</span>
###xml 632 655 <span type="species:ncbi:1299">Deinococcus radiodurans</span>
###xml 657 679 <span type="species:ncbi:727">Haemophilus influenzae</span>
###xml 681 705 <span type="species:ncbi:95486">Burkholderia cenocepacia</span>
###xml 728 737 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 1113 1131 <span type="species:ncbi:37372">Helicobacter bilis</span>
The genome of the A. butzleri strain RM4018 is predicted to contain a prophage. The size of this prophage is approximately 38 kb and spans genes ab1655-ab1706. BLASTP comparison of the predicted phage proteins to proteins from other bacteriophage indicates that this prophage is a member of the mutator (Mu) bacteriophage family. The size of the prophage is similar to other Mu-like bacteriophage, and it contains proteins similar to the Mu transposition proteins A and B in addition to coat, baseplate, and tail proteins. Mu-like bacteriophage have been found in multiple bacterial taxa, including E. coli, Neisseria meningitidis, Deinococcus radiodurans, Haemophilus influenzae, Burkholderia cenocepacia[96], [97] and notably C. jejuni (CMLP1: strain RM1221[52], [93]). Indeed, 26 of the 50 predicted RM4018 Mu-like phage proteins are similar to those encoded by CMLP1 (Table S2). Hence, it is proposed to name this bacteriophage AMLP1 (Arcobacter Mu-like phage). Mu-like bacteriophage have been identified in other epsilonproteobacterial taxa, including Campylobacter (11 species), Arcobacter (3 species), and Helicobacter bilis ([93]; Miller and Mendoza, unpublished data). Some of these Mu-like phage are similar to CMLP1, but many show marked variation in gene content and gene sequence, indicating that CMLP1 and AMLP1 are members of a diverse Mu bacteriophage family common to Proteobacteria.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 106 107 106 107 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</underline>
###xml 117 118 117 118 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</underline>
###xml 106 125 106 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><underline>A</underline>rcobacter <underline>b</underline>utzleri</italic>
###xml 125 126 125 126 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</underline>
###xml 133 134 133 134 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</underline>
###xml 209 215 209 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1330</italic>
###xml 216 222 216 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1358</italic>
###xml 292 298 292 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1721</italic>
###xml 299 305 299 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab1733</italic>
###xml 377 383 377 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab2090</italic>
###xml 384 390 384 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab2097</italic>
###xml 589 598 589 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 617 621 617 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Fouts1">[52]</xref>
###xml 624 636 624 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H. hepaticus</italic>
###xml 644 648 644 648 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Suerbaum1">[57]</xref>
###xml 654 663 654 663 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H. pylori</italic>
###xml 665 668 665 668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cag</italic>
###xml 673 677 673 677 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Tomb1">[58]</xref>
###xml 811 815 811 815 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Fouts1">[52]</xref>
###xml 817 821 817 821 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Parker2">[93]</xref>
###xml 843 852 843 852 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 1200 1207 1200 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. coli</italic>
###xml 1234 1238 1234 1238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Fouts1">[52]</xref>
###xml 1240 1244 1240 1244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Parker2">[93]</xref>
###xml 589 598 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 624 636 <span type="species:ncbi:32025">H. hepaticus</span>
###xml 654 663 <span type="species:ncbi:210">H. pylori</span>
###xml 843 852 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 1200 1207 <span type="species:ncbi:195">C. coli</span>
The genome of strain RM4018 also contains three small genomic islands, termed ABGI1, ABGI2 and ABGI3 (for Arcobacter butzlerigenomic island). ABGI1 is 26,918 bp (bp 1,324,568-1,351,485) and contains 29 genes (ab1330-ab1358). ABGI2 is 15,973 bp (bp 1,703,320-1,719,292) and contains 13 genes (ab1721-ab1733). ABGI3 is 4,907 bp (bp 2,103,976-2,108,882) and contains eight genes (ab2090-ab2097). Additionally, ABGI1-3 are bordered by direct repeats of 21, 21 and 25 bp, respectively. The presence of genomic islands within the epsilon subdivision is not unusual. They have been identified in C. jejuni (CJIE2 and CJIE3; [52]), H. hepaticus (HHGI; [57]) and H. pylori (cagPAI; [58]). CJIE2 and CJIE3 are bounded by direct repeats, contain an integrase gene at one end, and have integrated into the 3' end of a tRNA [52], [93]. Consistent with the C. jejuni islands, all three RM4018 genomic islands contain terminal integrase genes and ABGI1 has inserted into the 3' end of a leucinyl-tRNA; however, ABGI2 and ABGI3 did not integrate into tRNAs, although ABGI3 is in close proximity to a cysteinyl-tRNA. CJIE3 has been proposed to be an integrated plasmid, based on the similarity of this element to the C. coli strain RM2228 megaplasmid [52], [93]; in contrast, none of the protein functions encoded by elements ABGI1-3 suggested a plasmid origin. Interestingly, ABGI2 does encode proteins similar to the Type I restriction enzymes HsdS and HsdM. Thus, the only Type I, II, or III restriction/modification enzymes present in strain RM4018 are encoded by a genomic island. The role of ABGI3 is unknown.
###end p 72
###begin title 73
Antibiotic resistance
###end title 73
###begin p 74
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 102 110 102 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s006">Table S4</xref>
###xml 200 207 200 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. coli</italic>
###xml 275 279 275 279 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Fouts1">[52]</xref>
###xml 284 292 284 292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s006">Table S4</xref>
###xml 720 731 714 725 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 807 811 801 805 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Atabay2">[98]</xref>
###xml 0 33 <span type="species:ncbi:367737">Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018</span>
###xml 200 207 <span type="species:ncbi:195">C. coli</span>
###xml 720 731 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Arcobacter butzleri strain RM4018 was resistant to 42 of the 65 antibiotics tested (see supplementary Table S4). This level of resistance is remarkably high, considering that the multi-drug-resistant C. coli strain RM2228 was resistant to only 33 of the same 65 antibiotics ([52] and Table S4). Strain RM4018 was resistant to all macrolides and sulfonamides tested and to all of the beta-lactam antibiotics, with the exception of the beta-lactam cephalosporin ceftazidime. Strain RM4018 had resistance to some quinolones, i.e. nalidixic acid and oxolinic acid, and also to chloramphenicol and 5-fluorouracil (5FU). The pattern of antibiotic resistance in strain RM4018 is consistent, in part, with the resistances of 39 A. butzleri strains tested against a smaller set of 23 antibiotics by Atabay and Aydin [98], with the exception that strain RM4018 was resistant to chloramphenicol and nalidixic acid. No plasmids were detected in strain RM4018; therefore all resistance mechanisms would be chromosomal in nature.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 252 255 252 255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cat</italic>
###xml 262 268 262 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0785</italic>
###xml 526 531 517 522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lrgAB</italic>
###xml 540 546 531 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0179</italic>
###xml 548 554 539 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0180</italic>
###xml 596 610 587 601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staphylococcus</italic>
###xml 610 614 601 605 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Bayles1">[99]</xref>
###xml 616 621 607 612 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Groicher1">[100]</xref>
###xml 672 675 663 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">upp</italic>
###xml 824 827 815 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">upp</italic>
###xml 885 890 876 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Glaab1">[101]</xref>
###xml 892 897 883 888 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Martinussen1">[102]</xref>
###xml 920 923 911 914 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">upp</italic>
###xml 927 938 918 929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 252 255 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">cat</span>
###xml 927 938 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
In many cases, the antibiotic resistance observed for strain RM4018 was due to the presence or absence of genes characterized previously in terms of antibiotic resistance. For example, chloramphenicol resistance is due most likely to the presence of a cat gene (ab0785), which encodes a chloramphenicol O-acetyltransferase. beta-lactam resistance is due probably to the three putative beta-lactamases (AB0578, AB1306 and AB1486) present in the RM4018 genome; beta-lactam resistance may be enhanced also by the presence of the lrgAB operon (ab0179, ab0180) which modulates penicillin tolerance in Staphylococcus[99], [100]. Uracil phosphoribosyltransferase, encoded by the upp gene, catalyzes the first step in the pathway that leads to the production of the toxic analog 5-fluorodeoxyuridine monophosphate; mutations in the upp gene have been shown to lead to increased 5FU resistance [101], [102]. Thus, the absence of upp in A. butzleri strain RM4018 results presumably in high 5FU resistance.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 91 104 91 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 104 109 104 109 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Taylor2">[103]</xref>
###xml 114 124 114 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 124 129 124 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Abdelbaqi1">[104]</xref>
###xml 696 701 696 701 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Ruiz1">[105]</xref>
###xml 829 834 829 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Ruiz1">[105]</xref>
###xml 1250 1271 1250 1271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staphylococcus aureus</italic>
###xml 1351 1356 1351 1356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Yoshida1">[106]</xref>
###xml 1250 1271 <span type="species:ncbi:1280">Staphylococcus aureus</span>
Although strain RM4018 is resistant to some quinolones, mutations implicated previously in Campylobacter[103] and Arcobacter[104] quinolone resistance at Thr-86, Asp-90 and Ala-70 in the DNA gyrase subunit GyrA are not present in strain RM4018. It is probably not a coincidence that strain RM4018 is susceptible to hydrophilic quinolones (e.g. ciprofloxacin and norfloxacin) and resistant to hydrophobic ones (e.g. nalidixic acid and oxolinic acid). These data suggest that the mechanism of quinolone resistance in strain RM4018 is not at the level of the gyrase, but rather of uptake. Decreased quinolone uptake is associated with either increased impermeability or the activity of efflux pumps [105]. Hydrophobic quinolones alone can transit across the phospholipid bilayer but all quinolones can enter the cell through porins [105]. It is possible that the phospholipid bilayer of strain RM4018 has reduced permeability towards hydrophobic quinolones in conjunction with modifications in the porins to permit passage of only hydrophilic quinolones. A more likely scenario is the presence of a hydrophobic quinolone-specific efflux pump. Examples of pumps with specificity towards one class of quinolone are known; for example, the NorA protein of Staphylococcus aureus has been shown to be involved in the specific efflux of hydrophilic quinolones [106].
###end p 76
###begin title 77
Virulence determinants
###end title 77
###begin p 78
###xml 56 69 56 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 128 140 128 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri.</italic>
###xml 179 190 179 190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 240 244 240 244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Forsythe1">[10]</xref>
###xml 277 286 277 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 323 333 323 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 386 395 386 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 418 429 418 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 885 896 885 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 941 954 941 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 128 139 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 179 190 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 277 286 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 386 395 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 418 429 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 885 896 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Putative virulence determinants have been identified in Campylobacter, but little is known about potential virulence factors in A. butzleri. Since campylobacterioses and reported A. butzleri-related illnesses have similar clinical outcomes [10], it might be expected that some C. jejuni virulence factors would be found in Arcobacter. In fact, some virulence determinants identified in C. jejuni, have homologs within A. butzleri. For example, the fibronectin binding proteins CadF and Cj1349 have homologs in strain RM4018 (AB0483 and AB0070, respectively). Moreover, homologs of the invasin protein CiaB, the virulence factor MviN, the phospholipase PldA and the TlyA hemolysin are present in strain RM4018 (AB1555, AB0876, AB0859 and AB1846, respectively). However, it has not been determined if these putative virulence determinants are functional or if their function and role in A. butzleri biology is similar to the function of their Campylobacter homologs.
###end p 78
###begin p 79
###xml 27 40 27 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 176 182 176 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdtABC</italic>
###xml 285 286 285 286 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 291 292 291 292 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 299 304 299 304 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Pickett1">[107]</xref>
###xml 306 312 306 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdtABC</italic>
###xml 343 365 343 365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter hepaticus</italic>
###xml 392 405 392 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 430 436 430 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdtABC</italic>
###xml 505 510 505 510 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Johnson1">[108]</xref>
###xml 538 541 538 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdt</italic>
###xml 551 561 551 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter</italic>
###xml 570 581 570 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 643 648 643 648 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Jin1">[109]</xref>
###xml 650 655 650 655 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Pei1">[110]</xref>
###xml 343 365 <span type="species:ncbi:32025">Helicobacter hepaticus</span>
###xml 570 581 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
On the other hand, several Campylobacter virulence-associated genes are not present in the RM4018 genome. Most notably, the genes encoding the cytolethal distending toxin CDT (cdtABC) are absent from strain RM4018. CDT is an exotoxin which irreversibly blocks eukaryotic cells in the G1 or G2 phase [107]; cdtABC genes have been identified in Helicobacter hepaticus and several characterized Campylobacter genomes. The absence of cdtABC in strain RM4018 correlated well with a study by Johnson and Murano [108] which was unable to detect cdt genes in Arcobacter by PCR. A. butzleri strain RM4018 also contains no PEB1 or JlpA adhesin homologs [109], [110].
###end p 79
###begin p 80
###xml 96 100 96 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">irgA</italic>
###xml 102 108 102 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0729</italic>
###xml 114 119 114 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hecAB</italic>
###xml 121 127 121 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0941</italic>
###xml 128 134 128 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0940</italic>
###xml 141 145 141 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">irgA</italic>
###xml 154 165 154 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V. cholerae</italic>
###xml 215 220 215 220 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Goldberg1">[111]</xref>
###xml 344 351 344 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 351 356 351 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Johnson2">[112]</xref>
###xml 370 374 370 374 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">irgA</italic>
###xml 378 384 378 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ab0730</italic>
###xml 484 491 484 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 491 496 491 496 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Larsen1">[113]</xref>
###xml 606 610 606 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hecB</italic>
###xml 747 768 747 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Erwinia crysthanthemi</italic>
###xml 858 863 858 863 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Rojas1">[114]</xref>
###xml 943 963 943 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas syringae</italic>
###xml 965 987 965 987 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ralstonia solanacearum</italic>
###xml 1011 1031 1011 1031 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Burkholderia cepacia</italic>
###xml 1033 1050 1033 1050 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Acinetobacter spp</italic>
###xml 1070 1077 1070 1077 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 154 165 <span type="species:ncbi:666">V. cholerae</span>
###xml 344 351 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 484 491 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 943 963 <span type="species:ncbi:317">Pseudomonas syringae</span>
###xml 965 987 <span type="species:ncbi:305">Ralstonia solanacearum</span>
###xml 1011 1031 <span type="species:ncbi:292">Burkholderia cepacia</span>
###xml 1070 1077 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Analysis of the strain RM4018 genome identified two additional putative virulence determinants: irgA (ab0729) and hecAB (ab0941-ab0940). The irgA gene in V. cholerae encodes an iron-regulated outer membrane protein [111], and an IrgA homolog has been demonstrated to play a role in the pathogenesis of urinary tract infections by uropathogenic E. coli[112]. Adjacent to irgA is ab0730, which encodes a putative IroE homolog. IroE is a siderophore esterase found also in uropathogenic E. coli[113]. The other novel virulence determinant, HecA, is a member of the filamentous hemagglutinin (FHA) family, and hecB encodes a related hemolysin activation protein. FHA proteins are distributed widely among both plant and animal pathogens, e.g. HecA in Erwinia crysthanthemi contributes to both attachment and aggregation and is involved in epidermal cell killing [114]. Consistent with this distribution, RM4018 HecA homologs occur in both plant- (Pseudomonas syringae, Ralstonia solanacearum) and animal-pathogens (Burkholderia cepacia, Acinetobacter spp. and uropathogenic E. coli).
###end p 80
###begin title 81
Interacting with the environment: chemotaxis and signal transduction
###end title 81
###begin p 82
Microbial life is characterized by continuous interactions between bacteria and their environment. The ability of microorganisms to monitor environmental parameters is a prerequisite for survival. Hence, bacteria have evolved different mechanisms such as sensory histidine kinases, methyl-accepting chemotaxis proteins, sigma(sigma)/anti-sigma factor pairs, and adenylate and diguanylate cyclases to monitor and rapidly adapt to changes in their environment.
###end p 82
###begin p 83
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arcobacter butzleri</italic>
###xml 352 363 352 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 463 471 463 471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s004">Table S2</xref>
###xml 0 19 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">Arcobacter butzleri</span>
###xml 352 363 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Arcobacter butzleri is well equipped with a large number of these systems, allowing it to survive in diverse ecological niches. Prime bacterial mechanisms of environmental adaptation and gene regulation are the two-component systems (2CS), consisting of a membrane-bound sensor histidine protein kinase (HPK) and a cytoplasmic response regulator (RR). A. butzleri has one of the highest densities of 2CS genes per megabase, with a total of 78 genes of this type (Table S2). Analysis of the genome sequence revealed 36 HPK genes, 41 RR genes, and one hybrid HPK/RR gene. On the genome, 31 pairs of HPK and RR genes are present that likely form functional 2CS involved in responses to environmental changes. In three instances, a more complex regulation may exist, where an additional sensor or response regulator gene is adjacent to the pair, namely AB0416, AB0417, AB0418; AB0453, AB0454, AB0455; and AB0795, AB0796, AB0797.
###end p 83
###begin p 84
###xml 82 93 82 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 228 239 228 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 496 509 496 509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 570 575 570 575 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Korolik1">[115]</xref>
###xml 597 608 597 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 648 659 648 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 737 746 737 746 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. jejuni</italic>
###xml 800 805 800 805 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Korolik1">[115]</xref>
###xml 869 880 869 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1309 1314 1309 1314 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Szurmant1">[116]</xref>
###xml 1413 1418 1413 1418 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Szurmant1">[116]</xref>
###xml 1576 1581 1576 1581 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Tsang1">[117]</xref>
###xml 1621 1632 1621 1632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1760 1762 1760 1762 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</underline>
###xml 1762 1764 1762 1764 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1778 1781 1778 1781 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">che</underline>
###xml 1852 1857 1852 1857 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Anantharaman1">[118]</xref>
###xml 1916 1918 1916 1918 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 2101 2112 2101 2112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 82 93 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 228 239 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 597 608 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 648 659 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 737 746 <span type="species:ncbi:197">C. jejuni</span>
###xml 869 880 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1621 1632 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 2101 2112 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
A fully functional chemotaxis system modulated by the 2CS CheA-CheY is present in A. butzleri strain RM4018. Its genome encodes a large number of putative chemotaxis proteins, many of which are novel in the epsilon subdivision. A. butzleri is predicted to have the CheA, CheY, CheV, CheW, CheR and CheB core enzymes, although most of these proteins have low similarity to their epsilonproteobacterial orthologs, and some have key differences in terms of domain composition. For instance, CheA in Campylobacter spp. is fused to a CheY-like response regulator (RR) domain [115] which is absent from A. butzleri CheA. Also, the methylesterase CheB in A. butzleri has both the C-terminal methylesterase and N-terminal RR domains whereas the C. jejuni CheB protein contains only the methylesterase domain [115]. The presence of this CheB RR domain may support adaptation in A. butzleri, allowing the cell to "sense" increasing concentrations of attractants. In addition to these core chemotaxis proteins, strain RM4018 is predicted to encode the CheC phosphatase, the CheD glutamine amidase, involved in maturation of the methyl-accepting chemotaxis proteins (MCPs), and two additional CheY proteins. CheC hydrolyzes phosphorylated CheY and is employed by multiple taxa as an alternative to CheZ in signal removal [116]. The additional CheY proteins also could modulate signal removal by serving as a "phosphate sink" [116]. In the chemotaxis network, the receptor and kinase functions are separated in order to allow the cell to execute an integrated response to multiple stimuli [117]. The elaborate sensing capabilities of A. butzleri are reflected also in its high number (N = 25) of chemotaxis-specific receptors (MCPs). Some MCPs, e.g. AB1764, contain Cache (Ca2+ channels and chemotaxis) domains which have been identified in multiple bacterial taxa [118], and are similar to those found in animal voltage-gated Ca2+ channels. In addition, the periplasmic sensor region of AB1496 contains a putative nitrate/nitrite sensory domain, suggesting that nitrate and/or nitrite serves as an attractant for A. butzleri.
###end p 84
###begin p 85
###xml 78 89 78 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 554 565 550 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 632 643 628 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 853 858 849 854 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Niehus1">[119]</xref>
###xml 860 865 856 861 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Wosten1">[120]</xref>
###xml 881 892 877 888 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1089 1096 1085 1092 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1096 1101 1092 1097 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Chilcott1">[121]</xref>
###xml 1163 1185 1159 1181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sinorhizobium meliloti</italic>
###xml 1192 1197 1188 1193 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Sourjik1">[122]</xref>
###xml 78 89 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 554 565 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 632 643 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 881 892 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1089 1096 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1163 1185 <span type="species:ncbi:382">Sinorhizobium meliloti</span>
The limited similarity between the remaining non-chemotaxis-associated 2CS of A. butzleri and those of other bacteria do not allow functional prediction. However, six histidine kinases possess PAS domains, which are involved often in sensing changes in cellular energy levels, oxygen levels, or redox potential. Remarkable is the apparent lack of genes encoding homologs of the NtrC/NtrB family of two-component proteins that act together with the sigma factor RpoN. Genes encoding RpoN as well as the flagellar sigma factor FliA are also missing in the A. butzleri genome. This indicates that the transcriptional regulation of the A. butzleri polar flagella machinery is completely different from that of other Epsilonproteobacteria where the 2CS FlgS/FlgR together with RpoN and FliA regulate the formation of the basal-body hook and filament complex [119], [120]. Regulation of A. butzleri flagella synthesis may involve a completely novel system, since also absent from the genome are genes encoding homologs of the lateral master flagella transcription factors, such as FlhC, FlhD of E. coli[121] or members of the LuxR-type of transcription regulators like Sinorhizobium meliloti VisNR [122].
###end p 85
###begin p 86
###xml 54 65 54 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 109 122 109 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter</italic>
###xml 131 143 131 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter</italic>
###xml 180 181 180 181 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</underline>
###xml 185 186 185 186 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</underline>
###xml 197 198 197 198 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</underline>
###xml 407 412 391 396 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Hughes1">[123]</xref>
###xml 432 447 416 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">W. succinogenes</italic>
###xml 607 618 587 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 834 839 806 811 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Hughes1">[123]</xref>
###xml 884 895 856 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. enterica</italic>
###xml 897 910 869 882 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 915 930 887 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M. tuberculosis</italic>
###xml 930 935 902 907 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Kazmierczak1">[124]</xref>
###xml 54 65 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 432 447 <span type="species:ncbi:844">W. succinogenes</span>
###xml 607 618 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 884 895 <span type="species:ncbi:28901">S. enterica</span>
###xml 897 910 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 915 930 <span type="species:ncbi:1773">M. tuberculosis</span>
There are no predicted alternate sigma factors in the A. butzleri genome. Instead, and unlike the genomes of Campylobacter spp. or Helicobacter spp., it contains seven ECF-family (extracytoplasmic function) sigma/anti-sigma factor pairs. Genes encoding these pairs are in tandem. Anti-sigma factors are usually membrane-bound and prevent their cognate sigma factor from associating with core RNA polymerase [123]. To date, only the W. succinogenes proteins WS1422 and WS1423 have been identified as an ECF-family sigma factor pair within the epsilon subdivision. It is not known what genes are regulated in A. butzleri by these ECF-family sigma factors. In other bacterial taxa, these ECF-family sigma factors regulate functions such as alginate biosynthesis, iron-citrate transport, pyoverdine biosynthesis and cytochrome expression [123], and have been associated with virulence in S. enterica, P. aeruginosa and M. tuberculosis[124].
###end p 86
###begin p 87
###xml 9 20 9 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 483 488 483 488 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Romling1">[125]</xref>
###xml 490 495 490 495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Romling2">[126]</xref>
###xml 638 648 638 648 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s002">Figure S2b</xref>
###xml 738 743 738 743 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Gjermansen1">[127]</xref>
###xml 745 750 745 750 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-DaRe1">[128]</xref>
###xml 761 766 761 766 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Kazmierczak2">[129]</xref>
###xml 768 773 768 773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-OSheaT1">[130]</xref>
###xml 788 793 788 793 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Tischler1">[131]</xref>
###xml 9 20 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Finally, A. butzleri strain RM4018 encodes a class of proteins involved in formation and turnover of the "second messenger" bis-(3'-5')-cyclic dimeric guanosine monophosphate (cyclic-di-GMP). In bacteria cyclic-di-GMP is synthesized by diguanylate cyclases containing a conserved GGDEF motif (GGDEF(DUF1) domain proteins) and degraded into diguanylate (pGpG) by phosphodiesterase proteins containing domains enriched in glutamic acid, alanine and leucine (EAL(DUF2) domain proteins) [125], [126]. The genome of strain RM4018 encodes 25 proteins, either membrane-associated or cytoplasmic/periplasmic, containing GGDEF and/or EAL domains (Figure S2b). In other bacteria, GGDEF/EAL domain proteins have been implicated in biofilm formation [127], [128], motility [129], [130] and virulence [131].
###end p 87
###begin p 88
It is likely that many of the signal transduction proteins described above interact across group boundaries, e.g. GGDEF proteins with chemotaxis proteins. Thus, taken together, the large repertoire of 2C systems, chemotaxis proteins, ECF sigma factors and cyclic-di-GMP factors suggest the presence of a truly complex signal transduction network.
###end p 88
###begin title 89
###xml 31 42 31 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 31 42 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
Genomic comparisons with other A. butzleri strains
###end title 89
###begin p 90
###xml 28 39 28 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 223 230 223 230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0001358-t004">Table 4</xref>
###xml 296 307 296 307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 331 342 331 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 532 543 532 543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 594 599 594 599 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Pearson2">[132]</xref>
###xml 601 606 601 606 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0001358-Pin1">[133]</xref>
###xml 675 686 675 686 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 816 824 816 824 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s007">Table S5</xref>
###xml 929 940 929 940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1003 1014 1003 1014 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 1030 1038 1030 1038 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0001358.s008">Table S6</xref>
###xml 28 39 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 57 62 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 296 307 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 331 342 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 532 543 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 675 686 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 929 940 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
###xml 1003 1014 <span type="species:ncbi:28197">A. butzleri</span>
The genomic diversity of 13 A. butzleri strains, of both human and animal origin, was examined by microarray-based comparative genomic indexing (CGI) analysis. A list of the strains used in the CGI analysis is presented in Table 4. The CGI analysis allowed the assessment of CDS content for each A. butzleri strain relative to the A. butzleri DNA microarray, which comprises 2238 CDS from strain RM4018. Genomic DNA from strain RM4018 was used as a reference DNA and competitively hybridized with genomic DNA from each of the other A. butzleri strains. The GENCOM software described previously [132], [133] was used to assign the CDS as present, absent or multicopy for each A. butzleri strain. The complete CGI data sets as trinary scores (present = 1; absent = 0; and multicopy = 2) are available in supplementary Table S5. It was observed that 74.9% (1676 of 2238) of the CDS represented on the microarray were present in all A. butzleri strains, and served to define approximately the core genes of A. butzleri (supplementary Table S6).
###end p 90
###begin title 91
Strains used in the comparative genomic indexing analysis.
###end title 91
###begin p 92
All test strains selected had unique MLST sequence types (data not shown).
###end p 92
###begin p 93
###xml 93 104 93 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
###xml 118 129 118 129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. butzleri</italic>
